which constructors cannot be moved to gpu\n        cannot_move_to_gpu = OrderedSet[fx.Node]()\n\n        # For any node in the graph, which constructors does it have a dependency on\n        constructor_dependencies: dict[fx.Node, OrderedSet[fx.Node]] = defaultdict(\n            OrderedSet\n        )\n\n        # if a cpu node has a dependency on two different cpu constructors,\n        # then if either constructor cannot be moved to gpu, the other cannot as well.\n        # In this case any node with a dependency on one will have a dependency on the other\n        equal_constructor_sets: dict[fx.Node, OrderedSet[fx.Node]] = {\n            c: OrderedSet([c]) for c in constructors\n        }\n\n        def make_dependencies_equivalent(\n            set1: OrderedSet[fx.Node], set2: OrderedSet[fx.Node]\n        ) -> OrderedSet[fx.Node]:\n            # could use union find but not worth complexity here\n            set1.update(set2)\n            for obj in set1:\n                equal_constructor_sets[obj] = set1\n            return set1\n\n        queue: list[fx.Node] = list(constructors)\n\n        for c in queue:\n            constructor_dependencies[c].add(c)\n\n        while queue:\n            node = queue.pop()\n            dependencies = constructor_dependencies[node]\n\n            for user in node.users:\n                if self.cannot_be_moved(user):\n                    cannot_move_to_gpu.update(dependencies)\n                    break\n\n                # this node was used on a op which takes in multiple devices and output a gpu\n                # tensor. we can convert its cpu input to gpu without making further changes\n                if self.allow_cpu_device(user) and self.is_on_target_device(user):\n                    del cpu_indeg[user]\n                elif (\n                    self.allow_inputs\n                    and self.all_inputs_are_cpu_scalar_or_on_target_device(user)\n                ):\n                    # this node takes only cpu scalar tensors or gpu tensors as inputs\n                    # and outputs a gpu tensor. we can convert its cpu scalar inputs to gpu\n                    # without making further changes\n                    del cpu_indeg[user]\n                else:\n                    # otherwise, we should continue look at its downstream uses\n                    cpu_indeg[user] -= 1\n                    if cpu_indeg[user] == 0:\n                        del cpu_indeg[user]\n                        queue.append(user)\n\n                unioned_set = make_dependencies_equivalent(\n                    dependencies, constructor_dependencies[user]\n                )\n                constructor_dependencies[user] = unioned_set\n\n        for node in cpu_indeg:\n            if constructor_dependencies[node]:\n                cannot_move_to_gpu.update(constructor_dependencies[node])\n\n        all_cannot_move_to_gpu = cannot_move_to_gpu.copy()\n        for constructor in cannot_move_to_gpu:\n            all_cannot_move_to_gpu.update(equal_constructor_sets[constructor])\n\n        return OrderedSet(constructors) - all_cannot_move_to_gpu\n\n\ndef move_constructors_to_gpu(graph: fx.Graph) -> None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Moves intermediary tensors which are constructed on the cpu to gpu when safe\n    \"\"\"\n\n    # cudagraph does not support cpu tensors. In this pass, we update the graph\n    # by explicitly moving cpu scalar tensors to gpu when profitable, relying on\n    # graph partition to split off this data copy, and cudagraphifying\n    # the remaining gpu ops.\n    allow_inputs_outputs = bool(\n        torch._inductor.config.triton.cudagraphs\n        and torch._inductor.config.graph_partition\n    )\n    ConstructorMoverPass(\n        get_gpu_type(),\n        allow_inputs=allow_inputs_outputs,\n        allow_outputs=allow_inputs_outputs,\n    )(graph)\n",

torch.ops.aten.slice_scatter.default,\n        )\n\n    def is_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        node_device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        return node_device is not None and node_device.type == self.target\n\n    def is_cpu_scalar_tensor(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n target device.\n\n        If this function returns False, it means that this node and all of its users\n        won't be moved into the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        if node.target == ten.device\n\n    def get_cpu_indeg_count(self, graph: fx.Graph) -> dict[fx.Node, int]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Get the number of cpu inputs to a node\n        \"\"\"\n        cpu_indeg: self.get_node_device(node)\n            if device and device.type == self.target:\n                target_devices.add(device)\n\n            if (\n                self.allow_inputs\n    continue\n\n            if not (\n                isinstance(node.target, torch._ops.OpOverload)\n                and node.target.namespace in (\"prims\", \"aten\")\n            ):\n             continue\n\n            constructors.append(node)\n\n        # not handling multiple target devices initially\n        if not constructors or len(target_devices) != 1:\n if a cpu node has a dependency on two different cpu constructors,\n        # then if either constructor cannot be moved to gpu, the other cannot as well.\n        # In this case any node with a dependency on one will have a dependency on the other\n        equal_constructor_sets: dict[fx.Node, OrderedSet[fx.Node]] = {\n            c: OrderedSet([c]) for c in constructors\n        }\n\n        def make_dependencies_equivalent(\n            set1: OrderedSet[fx.Node], set2: OrderedSet[fx.Node]\n        ) -> OrderedSet[fx.Node]:\n            # could use union find but not worth complexity here\n            set1.update(set2)\n            for obj in set1:\n                equal_constructor_sets[obj] = set1\n            return set1\n\n        queue: list[fx.Node] = list(constructors)\n\n        for c in queue:\n            constructor_dependencies[c].add(c)\n\n        while queue:\n            node = queue.pop()\n            dependencies = constructor_dependencies[node]\n\n            for user in node.users:\n                if self.cannot_be_moved(user):\n                    cannot_move_to_gpu.update(dependencies)\n                    break\n\n                # this node was used on a op which takes in multiple devices and output a gpu\n                # tensor. we can convert its cpu input to gpu without making further changes\n                if self.allow_cpu_device(user) and self.is_on_target_device(user):\n                    del cpu_indeg[user]\n                elif (\n                    self.allow_inputs\n                    and self.all_inputs_are_cpu_scalar_or_on_target_device(user)\n                ):\n                    # this node takes only cpu scalar tensors or gpu tensors as inputs\n                    # and outputs a gpu tensor. we can convert its cpu scalar inputs to gpu\n                    # without making further changes\n                    del cpu_indeg[user]\n                else:\n                    # import urllib.request
import urllib.error

def fetch_raw_file(repo, branch, file_path):
    """Fetch raw file content from GitHub"""
    url = f"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/sg-evals/pytorch--ca246612/{branch}/{file_path}"
    try:
        with urllib.request.urlopen(url) as response:
            return response.read().decode('utf-8')
    except urllib.error.HTTPError as e:
        print(f"Error fetching {file_path}: {e}")
        return None

# Try to fetch the files from GitHub
files = [
    ("torch/_inductor/fx_passes/post_grad.py", "master"),
    ("torch/_decomp/decompositions.py", "master"),
    ("test/inductor/test_pattern_matcher.py", "master"),
]

print("Attempting to fetch files from GitHub...")
for file_path, branch in files:
    content = fetch_raw_file("pytorch--ca246612", branch, file_path)
    if content:
        print(f"✓ Successfully fetched {file_path} ({len(content)} bytes)")
    else:
        print(f"✗ Failed to fetch {file_path}")

import urllib.request
import os

def fetch_raw_file(file_path):
    """Fetch raw file content from GitHub"""
    url = f"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/sg-evals/pytorch--ca246612/master/{file_path}"
    with urllib.request.urlopen(url) as response:
        return response.read().decode('utf-8')

# 1. Modify torch/_inductor/fx_passes/post_grad.py
print("Processing post_grad.py...")
post_grad_content = fetch_raw_file("torch/_inductor/fx_passes/post_grad.py")
lines = post_grad_content.split('\n')

# Remove lines 684-741 (the function definition) and line 769 (the call)
# Since we're removing 58 lines (684-741), line 769 becomes 769-58=711
# But we need to be careful about the exact indices
# Lines to remove: 684-741 (58 lines) and then adjust for the call

new_lines = lines[:684] + lines[742:]  # Remove function definition

# Now find and remove the call to register_addmm_activation_fusions
# After removing 58 lines, line 770 becomes 770-58=712
# But we need to find the line dynamically
final_lines = []
for i, line in enumerate(new_lines):
    if "register_addmm_activation_fusions()" not in line:
        final_lines.append(line)
    else:
        print(f"Removing line {i}: {line.strip()}")

new_post_grad = '\n'.join(final_lines)

# Write to local file
os.makedirs('/workspace/torch/_inductor/fx_passes', exist_ok=True)
with open('/workspace/torch/_inductor/fx_passes/post_grad.py', 'w') as f:
    f.write(new_post_grad)

print(f"✓ Modified post_grad.py (original: {len(lines)} lines, new: {len(final_lines)} lines)")

import urllib.request
import os

def fetch_raw_file(file_path):
    """Fetch raw file content from GitHub"""
    url = f"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/sg-evals/pytorch--ca246612/master/{file_path}"
    with urllib.request.urlopen(url) as response:
        return response.read().decode('utf-8')

# 2. Modify torch/_decomp/decompositions.py
print("Processing decompositions.py...")
decomp_content = fetch_raw_file("torch/_decomp/decompositions.py")
lines = decomp_content.split('\n')

# Find the _addmm_activation function
# Looking for the @register_decomposition(aten._addmm_activation) decorator
start_idx = None
end_idx = None
for i, line in enumerate(lines):
    if '@register_decomposition(aten._addmm_activation)' in line:
        start_idx = i
    if start_idx is not None and i > start_idx and line.strip() and not line.startswith(' ') and not line.startswith('\t') and i > start_idx + 5:
        # Found the next function/decorator that's not indented
        if '@register_decomposition' in line or 'def ' in line:
            end_idx = i
            break

if start_idx is not None:
    # Find the start of the function by going backwards from the decorator
    func_start = start_idx
    while func_start > 0 and lines[func_start - 1].strip() == '':
        func_start -= 1
    
    # Find the end of the function
    if end_idx is None:
        for i in range(start_idx + 1, len(lines)):
            if lines[i].strip() and not lines[i].startswith(' ') and not lines[i].startswith('\t') and not lines[i].startswith('@'):
                end_idx = i
                break
    
    print(f"Found _addmm_activation function at lines {func_start}-{end_idx}")
    print(f"Start line: {lines[func_start][:80]}")
    if end_idx:
        print(f"End line {end_idx}: {lines[end_idx][:80]}")
    
    # Remove the function
    if end_idx:
        new_lines = lines[:func_start] + lines[end_idx:]
    else:
        new_lines = lines[:func_start]
else:
    print("Could not find _addmm_activation function")
    new_lines = lines

new_decomp = '\n'.join(new_lines)

# Write to local file
os.makedirs('/workspace/torch/_decomp', exist_ok=True)
with open('/workspace/torch/_decomp/decompositions.py', 'w') as f:
    f.write(new_decomp)

print(f"✓ Modified decompositions.py (original: {len(lines)} lines, new: {len(new_lines)} lines)")

import urllib.request

def fetch_raw_file(file_path):
    """Fetch raw file content from GitHub"""

# Find the test_addmm_activation_fusion method
test_start = None
test_end = None
for i, line in enumerate(lines):
    if 'def test_addmm_activation_fusion(self):' in line:
        # Go back to find the decorator
        test_start = i - 1
        while test_start > 0 and (lines[test_start].strip().startswith('@') or lines[test_start].strip() == ''):
            test_start -= 1
        test_start += 1
        break

if test_start is not None:
    # Find the end of the test method
    indent_level = len(lines[test_start + 1]) - len(lines[test_start + 1].lstrip())
    for i in range(test_start + 2, len(lines)):
        line = lines[i]
        if line.strip() == '':
            continue
        if line.startswith(' ' * indent_level) and not line.startswith(' ' * (indent_level + 1)):
            # Found the next method at the same indent level
            test_end = i
            break
    
    if test_end is None:
        test_end = len(lines)
    
    print(f"Found test_addmm_activation_fusion at lines {test_start}-{test_end}")
    
    # Remove the test method

else:
    print("Could not find test_addmm_activation_fusion method")
    new_lines = lines

import urllib.request
import os

def fetch_raw_file(file_path):
    url = f"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/sg-evals/pytorch--ca246612/master/{file_path}"
    with urllib.request.urlopen(url) as response:
        return response.read().decode('utf-8')

# Process test_pattern_matcher.py correctly
print("Processing test_pattern_matcher.py (final)...")
test_content = fetch_raw_file("test/inductor/test_pattern_matcher.py")
lines = test_content.split('\n')

# Find the test method
test_start = None
test_end = None

for i, line in enumerate(lines):
    if 'def test_addmm_activation_fusion(self):' in line:
        # Go back to find decorator(s)
        j = i - 1
        while j >= 0 and (lines[j].strip() == '' or lines[j].strip().startswith('@')):
            j -= 1
        test_start = j + 1
        
        # Go forward to find the next method
        for k in range(i + 1, len(lines)):
            # Check if this line starts a new method at same indentation
            if lines[k].startswith('    def '):
                test_end = k
                break
        
        break

if test_start is not None and test_end is not None:
    print(f"Removing lines {test_start} to {test_end-1}")
    print(f"Lines to remove:")
    for idx in range(test_start, min(test_start + 5, test_end)):
        print(f"  {idx}: {lines[idx][:70]}")
    print("  ...")
    for idx in range(max(test_start, test_end-3), test_end):
        print(f"  {idx}: {lines[idx][:70]}")
    
    new_lines = lines[:test_start] + lines[test_end:]
else:
    print("Could not find test method boundaries")
    new_lines = lines

new_test = '\n'.join(new_lines)

# Write to local file
with open('/workspace/test/inductor/test_pattern_matcher.py', 'w') as f:
    f.write(new_test)

print(f"✓ Modified test_pattern_matcher.py (original: {len(lines)} lines, new: {len(new_lines)} lines, removed: {len(lines)-len(new_lines)} lines)")
